Willing a Sinful Act for a Good Purpose
Maturidi addresses whether the Prophet's will for defeat of polytheists was a sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between intending an act that is sinful and intending sin itself, and how this applies to divine will and prophetic actions.

Core Idea
Willing an act that results in sin is not the same as willing sin.

Maturidi addresses a theological objection: Did the Prophet sin by willing the defeat of the polytheists? He clarifies that one can intend an act for a good purpose even if the act is sinful from a certain perspective. The key is the intention behind the will, not the outcome alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the jurist's question
Read the opening sentence to understand the objection: Is defeat (inhiyam) obedience or disobedience? The jurist presents a dilemma.
2
Follow the response and examples
Note how Maturidi (through the jurist's voice) replies that the act is disobedience but can be willed not for its sinfulness but for a benefit. Examine the Qur'anic example (5:29) and the analogy with believers' sins.
The distinction hinges on the intention (qasd) behind the will.
3
Apply the principle to divine will
Consider how Maturidi extends the argument to God's will: Allah wills the disbeliever's act of disbelief for some wisdom, not for the sin itself. This preserves divine justice.
This connects to the broader theological principle that God's will for an act does not imply He wills the sinfulness in it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فالانهزام طاعة أو معصية ؟ وكذلك الحال إلى وقت النظر ، وفى ذلك دوام على المعصية . لا بد أن يقول : معصية ، فيجوز أن يراد به لا على قصدها لبعض المصالح ، ومثله قوله : إِنِّي أُرِيدُ أَنْ تَبُوا بِإِثْمِي . إنه يجوز إرادة فعل هو معصية لا على قصد عصيان ، وكذلك وكذلك معاصي المؤمنين كلها كانت على أفعال من عاصيهم ، وإن لم يريدوا معصية الله ، بل لو أرادوا لكفروا ، فهذا يبين أن إرادة فعل يكون من فاعله معصية لا يكون كإرادة المعصية ، فمثله إرادة الله فعل الكافر ليكون منه معصية ، أو فعله الشتم ليكون مشتما قبيحا لا يكون كإرادة الشتم والمعصية ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The jurist (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Is defeat (inhiyam) obedience or disobedience? And similarly the situation until the time of consideration, and in that is persistence in disobedience. It must be said: Disobedience. Then it is permissible that it be intended not with the intention of it for some benefit. An example of that is His saying: 'I intend that you should bear my sin.' Indeed, it is permissible to intend an act that is disobedience not with the intention of disobedience. And likewise all the acts of disobedience of the believers were acts from those who disobeyed them, even though they did not intend disobedience to Allah; rather, if they had intended it, they would have disbelieved. This clarifies that the intention of an act that is disobedience from its doer is not like the intention of disobedience. Similarly, Allah's intention of the disbeliever's act to be disobedience from him, or His act of reviling to be reviling and ugly, is not like the intention of reviling and disobedience. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 897

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from a jurist (al-faqih) concerning the Prophet's desire for the defeat (inhiyam) of the polytheists. The jurist asks whether that defeat is obedience or disobedience. He argues that if it is disobedience, then it implies the Prophet intended a sinful outcome. Maturidi (via the jurist's voice?) clarifies that an act can be willed not for its sinful nature but for some other benefit. He cites the Qur'anic verse (5:29) where a person says 'I intend that you should bear my sin,' meaning the intention is for the other to bear it, not to commit sin per se. He then applies this to all sins of believers: they perform acts that are sinful but do not intend disobedience to God; if they intended disobedience, they would be disbelievers. Thus, the intention of an act that happens to be sinful is not the same as intending sin. Analogously, God's will for the disbeliever's act of disbelief is not an intention of sin; rather, He intends the act for some wisdom, while the sinfulness comes from the doer's side. The passage emphasizes that God's will for an act that is sinful is not like a creature's will for sin.

Key Terms
إرادة (will/intention)
معصية (disobedience/sin)
طاعة (obedience)
قصد (intention/purpose)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God wills a sinful act, He intends sin.
Correction: This passage clarifies that God's will is for the act's existence, not for its sinfulness. God intends the act for a wise purpose, while the sinfulness is attributed to the doer's free will.

Checkpoint
What is the key distinction Maturidi makes in this passage regarding divine will?
A) God's will is only for obedience, not for sinful acts.
B) Intending an act that results in sin is different from intending sin itself.
C) Sinful acts are never willed by God.
D) The Prophet's will for defeat was actually obedience.

Key Takeaway
The intention of an act that results in sin is distinct from intending sin itself, which preserves divine justice and prophetic impeccability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you committed a sin but told yourself it was for a 'good reason.' What was your actual intention? Were you truly aiming for the benefit, or were you deceiving yourself? This lesson demands you examine the state of your heart. Will you confess that to Allah and repent with sincerity?
?
Do you ever blame Allah for your sins, thinking He willed them so you are not responsible? This lesson clarifies that God's will for the act is not His intention for the sin. How will you take full ownership of your intentions from now on? What will you do the next time you feel tempted to shift blame?
?
If you believe that God is just, why do you still sin? Because you intend the act for some worldly gain, not the sin itself? Or because you simply ignore His commands? Let this lesson pierce your heart: your intention matters to God. Will you commit to checking your intentions before every action today?

Refuting the Claim of the Prophet's Pleasure with the Polytheists' Defeat
Maturidi refutes the claim that the Prophet's pleasure implies divine approval of the polytheists' defeat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's pleasure regarding the polytheists' defeat was not for the sake of Allah or the Prophet himself, thus the objection is invalid.

Core Idea
Pleasure in divine context depends on the purpose of the action, not mere outcome.

When an objector claimed that the Prophet was pleased with the defeat of the polytheists, implying that the defeat was divinely approved, Maturidi quickly counters by analyzing the object of that pleasure. He argues that the defeat was not for the Prophet or for God, so it cannot be framed in terms of divine pleasure or displeasure. This lesson unpacks that crisp rejoinder.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the objection and Maturidi's response.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the objection
The objector claims the Prophet was pleased (رضى) with the defeat. Why would that be problematic?
If the Prophet was pleased, doesn't that imply divine approval?
3
Analyze Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi says the defeat was not for the Prophet or Allah, so one cannot speak of pleasure/displeasure in that context.
He distinguishes between actions done for Allah and those that are not.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
This shows that divine pleasure is tied to the purpose and agent of the action, not just the outcome.
Consider how this relates to Maturidi's overall theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عارض بأن رسول الله رضى منهم . ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لأن الانهزام منهم لم يكن لرسول الله أو لله ، فيتكلم فيه بالرضا وغير الرضا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم عورض بما كان كفر أكثر عباد الله بأن أراد إبليس ، والله أراد منهم الطاعة ، فصارت إرادة إبليس فى ملك الله وسلطانه أبعد من إرادة الله ، فأجاب بالرضا والمحبة والسخط ، وقد بينا نحن الفصل بين الأمرين ، على أنه يكون فعل يرضى به المرء ويسخط من غير أن كان وقت فعله ، ومحال ذلك في الإرادة ثبت أنها شرط الفعل فيما يظهر التعجيز إذ لا يخلو عنها فعل المختار . وأيضا إنا لا نقول بأن الله يحب من يعلم أنه لا يؤمن أو يرضى منه لأنهما يحبان بالفعل ، فمن لا يفعل بالقول به بعيد ، وأما الإرادة فقد بينا ، والله أعلم .
Then he objected that the Messenger of Allah was pleased with them. And that is invalid because the defeat from them was not for the Messenger of Allah or for Allah, so one speaks about it with pleasure and displeasure. And there is no power except with Allah. Then he was objected to with the fact that the disbelief of most of Allah's servants was because Iblis willed, and Allah willed obedience from them, so the will of Iblis in the kingdom and authority of Allah is more distant from Allah's will. He answered by (the concepts of) pleasure, love, and anger. And we have already explained the distinction between the two matters: that there is an action that one is pleased with and angry at without it being at the time of its occurrence. That is impossible for will, it being established that will is a condition of action in what appears to be incapacity, since the action of the free agent cannot be free of it. Also, we do not say that Allah loves those whom He knows will not believe or is pleased with them, because these (love and pleasure) are with action. So whoever does not act is far from saying that. As for will, we have already explained. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 898

Commentary
This passage addresses two objections. First, an objector claims that the Prophet was pleased with the defeat of the polytheists, implying that the act was good. Maturidi refutes this by noting that the defeat was not for the Prophet or for God, so it cannot be said to be pleasing or displeasing in the same sense. Second, an objector argues that since Iblis willed disbelief for most people and God willed obedience from them, Iblis's will seems to prevail over God's will in His own kingdom. Maturidi answers by distinguishing between pleasure/love/anger and will. He explains that pleasure and anger can relate to an action after its occurrence without having caused it, but will is a condition for the action—a free agent's action cannot occur without will. Thus, God's will is efficient, whereas Iblis's will is not. Additionally, Maturidi clarifies that God does not love or feel pleasure toward those whom He knows will not believe, because love and pleasure are based on actual action, not mere preordination. The passage concludes by reaffirming the previous explanation about will.

Key Terms
رضا (pleasure/satisfaction)
إرادة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's personal emotions always indicate divine approval.
Correction: Maturidi shows that pleasure is context-dependent; not every event that pleases a human is divinely approved.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is the objection about the Prophet's pleasure invalid?
A) Because the Prophet never experienced pleasure at that event.
B) Because the defeat was not for the Prophet or Allah, so pleasure/displeasure cannot be attributed to it.
C) Because the Prophet's pleasure is irrelevant to divine will.
D) Because the polytheists' defeat was actually displeasing to the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's pleasure at an event does not automatically signify divine approval; the action's purpose and relation to Allah must be considered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel pleased about an outcome in your life, do you ever assume that God must be pleased too? How does this lesson challenge you to separate your emotions from divine approval?
?
Can you recall a situation where you were happy about something that later harmed your faith? What does that teach you about the need to evaluate events by their purpose and relation to Allah, not by your feelings?
?
The Prophet's pleasure at the polytheists' defeat could have been misunderstood as divine endorsement. What are some modern examples where people confuse human reactions with God's will? How can you guard your own heart against this error?

Distinguishing Divine Will from Pleasure in Responding to Iblis's Will Objection
Maturidi distinguishes will from pleasure/love to refute the objection about Iblis's will prevailing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's key distinction between will (which necessitates action) and pleasure/anger (which can be after action), and how this resolves the objection that Iblis's will appears stronger than God's.

Core Idea
Will is a condition for action; pleasure can come after without causing it.

A more serious objection arises: if Iblis wills disbelief for most people, and God wills obedience from them, then Iblis's will seems to prevail in God's own kingdom. Maturidi responds by drawing a sharp distinction between will, which is a necessary condition for the occurrence of an action, and attributes like pleasure and love, which can relate to an action after its occurrence. This lesson delves into that crucial theological distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the objection and Maturidi's answer.
The passage is longer and involves multiple concepts.
2
Identify the objection
The objector says: Iblis willed disbelief, God willed obedience, but disbelief happened. So Iblis's will seems more effective.
This challenges God's sovereignty.
3
Understand Maturidi's distinction
He introduces pleasure (رضا), love (محبة), and anger (سخط) as distinct from will. Pleasure can be after an action, but will is a condition of the action. So Iblis's will is not causal; only God's will is.
The key point: will must be present for an action to occur, but pleasure can be retrospective.
4
Apply the distinction
Thus, Iblis's will to disbelieve does not cause disbelief; rather, God's will permits it or decrees it. But God does not love or take pleasure in disbelief.
Maturidi adds that love and pleasure are based on actual action, not preordination.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
This preserves God's sovereignty and justice: He wills all that occurs, but He is not pleased with evil actions.
Consider how this relates to Maturidi's broader theology of free will and divine attributes.

This passage addresses two objections. First, an objector claims that the Prophet was pleased with the defeat of the polytheists, implying that the act was good. Maturidi refutes this by noting that the defeat was not for the Prophet or for God, so it cannot be said to be pleasing or displeasing in the same sense. Second, an objector argues that since Iblis willed disbelief for most people and God willed obedience from them, Iblis's will seems to prevail over God's will in His own kingdom. Divine Will: The Only Source of Human Action
Maturidi establishes that God's will is necessary for every voluntary human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that every human action must be by God's will, and how he refutes the Mu'tazila's denial of a distinct attribute of will.

Core Idea
Every action stems from will, compulsion, or forgetfulness—and only will fits God.

Maturidi begins with a simple observation about human actions: they always fall into one of three categories. He then applies this to God, showing that compulsion and forgetfulness are impossible for Him, so His will must be the source. He also addresses the Mu'tazila, who reduce will to mere knowledge, arguing that their position is inconsistent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three categories of action: will, compulsion, forgetfulness.
2
Understand the logical deduction
See why Maturidi eliminates compulsion and forgetfulness for God, leaving will as the only possibility.
Apply the principle that God cannot be described with imperfection.
3
Analyze the critique of Mu'tazila
Understand their view (will as mere knowledge) and Maturidi's counter-argument that this meaning exists in all actions.
Consider why their denial is inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل فى هذا فى المتعارف أن الفعل يخرج على إرادة أو غلبة أو غفلة ، الله سبحانه لا يجوز أن يوصف فى فعل العبد بالغلبة أو بالغفلة ، ثبت أن كان بالإرادة . والمعتزلة لا يثبتون لله معنى في الإرادة سوى كون العلم بعد يكن من غير ضرورة له ، وهذا المعنى هو فى فعل كل من أهل العالم قائم ، فلا وجه لإنكارهم على قولهم ، وبالله العصمة .
And the principle in this matter, according to common usage, is that action proceeds from either will, compulsion, or forgetfulness. Allah, exalted be He, cannot be described in the action of the servant with compulsion or forgetfulness. So it is established that it is by will. And the Mu'tazila do not affirm for Allah a meaning (ma'na) in will other than knowledge that it will be without necessity for Him. And this meaning exists in the action of everyone among the people. So there is no basis for their denial of their statement. And with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 898

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle: in common understanding, every action occurs either by will (irada), compulsion (ghalba), or forgetfulness (ghafla). Since it is impossible to attribute compulsion or forgetfulness to Allah in relation to the servant's action, it must be that the action occurs by Allah's will. This serves as a rational proof for the necessity of divine will. Maturidi then critiques the Mu'tazila, who deny that God has a distinct attribute of will. They consider will to be merely knowledge of the outcome without any need (gharar). Maturidi argues that this same meaning (of knowledge) exists in all people's actions, so their denial is inconsistent. The passage ends with a prayer for divine protection.

Key Terms
إرادة (will)
غلبة (compulsion/force)
غفلة (forgetfulness)
معنى (meaning/attribute)
معتزلة (Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Actions can occur without God's will.
Correction: Maturidi argues that every action must be by will, compulsion, or forgetfulness; since compulsion and forgetfulness are impossible for God, His will is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why must human actions be by God's will?
A) Because God is the only agent.
B) Because actions cannot proceed from compulsion or forgetfulness in God's case.
C) Because the Mu'tazila deny will.
D) Because the Qur'an says so.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates through a simple classification that God's will is the necessary source of every human action, because compulsion and forgetfulness are impossible for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a recent action of yours, perhaps a mistake or a moment of obedience. Do you truly believe that God's will was its sole source, or do you feel that your own will operated independently? How does the answer affect your sense of reliance on Him?
?
When you sin, do you ever think, 'God didn't will this for me'? If so, how does this passage challenge that belief? If you accept that God willed it, how do you reconcile that with your responsibility? What would change in your repentance if you fully internalized this truth?
?
The Mu'tazila made God's will a mere knowledge, perhaps to protect human responsibility. But does that protect God's perfection? Where in your life have you reduced God's attributes to fit your understanding, rather than submitting to His revelation? What step can you take today to affirm His will over your own?

Proof That God’s Will Is the Agent of Human Acts
Maturidi gives a proof and refutation on divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that human actions are caused by God's will through the elimination of force and heedlessness, and his refutation of the Mu'tazilite view that God's will is merely knowledge.

Core Idea
God's will is the only possible cause of human actions because compulsion and heedlessness are impossible for Him.

Imam Maturidi presents a concise proof that every act must arise from will, force, or heedlessness. Since God cannot be subject to force or heedlessness, human actions must be attributed to His will. He then addresses the Mu'tazilite objection that God's will is simply His knowledge, showing this view fails to distinguish divine will from human will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage contains two distinct moves: a proof and a refutation.
2
Identify the tripartite classification
The passage states that acts proceed from will, force, or heedlessness. Understand each term and why this classification is considered exhaustive for voluntary acts.
This is an empirical observation from common parlance.
3
Apply the classification to God
Since force and heedlessness are impossible for God, the only remaining cause is will. This is the core of the proof.
Ask yourself why force and heedlessness are impossible for God.
4
Examine the Mu'tazilite refutation
Maturidi criticizes the Mu'tazila for reducing God's will to mere knowledge. See why he finds this inadequate.
Consider how this argument defends the reality of God's attribute of will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا في المتعارف أن الفعل يخرج على إرادة أو غلبة أو غفلة، الله سبحانه لا يجوز أن يوصف في فعل العبد بالغلبة أو بالغفلة، ثبت أن كان بالإرادة. والمعتزلة لا يثبتون لله معنى في الإرادة سوى كون العلم بعد يكن من غير ضرورة له، وهذا المعنى هو في فعل كل من أهل العالم قائم، ثم فلا وجه لإنكارهم على قولهم، وبالله العصمة.
The principle regarding this in common parlance is that the act proceeds from will, force, or heedlessness. God, exalted, cannot be described with respect to the servant's act as having force or heedlessness, so it is established that it is by will. The Mu'tazila do not affirm for God a meaning in will beyond knowledge that it is [that the act will occur] without necessity for Him. But this meaning is present in the action of every inhabitant of the world. Then there is no basis for their denial of [this] statement. And with God is preservation.
Source pages p. 898

Commentary
This passage contains a rational proof and a refutation of the Mu'tazila. Maturidi begins by stating an empirical classification: in common experience, every voluntary act is caused either by will (irada), by compulsion (ghalaba), or by heedlessness (ghafla). Since God is absolutely free from compulsion and heedlessness, the only remaining possibility for His causing human acts is will. He then attacks the Mu'tazila position that God's will is merely knowledge of the act. Maturidi argues that such a notion of will is found in every human being (as knowledge of the act), so it fails to distinguish God's will. Hence, the Mu'tazila denial of a real attribute of will is unfounded.

Key Terms
إرادة
غلبة
غفلة
علم
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila belief that God's will is merely His knowledge of the act.
Correction: Maturidi argues that such a notion of will is present in every human, so it does not capture the distinctive nature of God's will.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why must human actions be attributed to God's will rather than force or heedlessness?
A) Because God is all-powerful.
B) Because force and heedlessness are impossible for God.
C) Because God knows everything.
D) Because human actions are free.

Key Takeaway
Human actions are caused by God's will because force and heedlessness cannot be attributed to God, and God's will is a real attribute distinct from mere knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action you do is ultimately caused by God's will, does that make you feel powerless or comforted? Why? How does this truth change the way you view your own successes and failures?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed God's will is just knowledge—are there areas of your life where you treat God's will as mere information rather than as the active cause of everything that happens? What would change if you truly believed His will is the real agent?
?
When you sin, do you ever feel God has left you? According to this passage, God's will is always the agent—so in your moments of disobedience, what does that say about His relationship to your sin? How does that challenge your assumptions about God's involvement in your life?

Divine Will vs. Wishful Thinking
Maturidi distinguishes divine will from wishful thinking and refutes coercion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine will is effective while Satan's wish is impotent, and why faith cannot be coerced.

Core Idea
Wishful thinking cannot overcome divine will; coercion invalidates faith.

Maturidi begins by addressing a key misunderstanding about the divine attribute of will. He contrasts the effective will of Allah with the mere wish of Iblis, showing that wishful thinking lacks the power to overcome divine determination. This distinction leads to a refutation of the idea that God could or should force belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the contrast between 'irāda' and 'tamannī'.
2
Identify the two wills
The passage mentions the will of Iblis (wishful thinking) and the will of Allah (effective). See how Maturidi uses a reported statement to set up the distinction.
3
Understand the objection and reply
Al-Faqih objects that if God can prevent disbelief, He should. The reply explains that will sometimes overcomes, but wish does not. Then it condemns faith by coercion as an effect of confusion.
This shows that divine power does not imply coercion.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why coercion is impermissible—faith must be chosen, not forced. The passage guards against the sectarian view that God compels disbelief.
This is a core Maturidi position on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : إرادة إبليس هي التمني ، ولو أراد العباد ما كفروا ، والله يقدر على منعهم بالقهر قال الفقيه رحمه الله : قلنا له قد صدقت، والإرادة قد توجب الغلبة والتمني لا ، فكيف غلب تمني عدوه على إرادته ؟ وقوله : يقدر ويقهر ، وهذا النوع إنما هو أثر الحيرة والوحشة ، ولا يجوز الإيمان بالقسر بوجه . ثم قال : فإن قيل : رأيت حكيما يقدر على منع عبده عن أمر لا يريده ولا يمنحه ؟ فعارض بالجبر ، وذا خطأ ؛ لأنه عندنا يريده ، وليس المنع من شرط ما يراد . ثم فإنه يعد لوجهين لا يريده ولا يجوز له المنع لضرب من التدبير قال الشيخ رحمه الله : إن كنت على الشاهد تقدره فلا تجاده ، إلا أن لا يقدر عليه أو هو لم يرد الفعل به . قال : ومنها ما يجب المنع ، فدل أن المنع إن وجب وجب لعلة لا لعينه ، وما يذكر من العلة فإن كانت أوجبت الاضطرار ، فهو الذي قيل لا يقدر عليه ، وإن كان لا يوجب ، وقد يملك القهر لا بالتعدى ، فهو لا يسعه عندنا ، وهو خارج من العرف ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then he said: The will of Iblis is wishful thinking. And if the servants had willed, they would not have disbelieved. And God is able to prevent them by force. Al-Faqih (may God have mercy on him) said: We said to him: You have spoken the truth. Will sometimes necessitates overcoming, but wishful thinking does not. So how did the wishful thinking of His enemy overcome His will? And His saying: "He is able and compels" – this type is only the effect of confusion and alienation, and faith through coercion is not permissible in any way. Then he said: If it is said: Do you see a wise person who is able to prevent his servant from something he does not will and does not grant him? He objected by coercion (jabr), and that is an error; because according to us, He wills it, and prevention is not a condition of what is willed. Then it is counted for two aspects: He does not will it, and it is not permissible for Him to prevent it for a kind of management. The Sheikh (may God have mercy on him) said: If you base it on the witnessed, you would not find it, unless He is not able to do it or He did not will the action by it. He said: Among them is what necessitates prevention. So it indicates that prevention, if it is necessary, is necessary for a cause, not for itself. And the cause mentioned, if it necessitates compulsion, then it is that which it was said He is not able to do. And if it does not necessitate, and He may possess force without transgression, then it is not within His capacity according to us, and it is outside of custom. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 899

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument defending divine predestination against the charge of coercion (jabr). It begins by distinguishing between divine will (إرادة), which is effective, and Satan's wish (تمني), which is impotent. The interlocutor objects that if God has power to prevent disbelief by force, He should do so. The answer states that faith by force is impermissible and would be an effect of confusion (حيرة) and alienation (وحشة). Another objection is raised: a wise master would prevent his servant from doing what he does not will; why doesn't God do likewise? The reply clarifies that God does will the servant's act, and prevention is not a necessary condition of what is willed. The sheikh then explains that prevention, when it occurs, is for a reason (علة), not arbitrarily. If the reason necessitates compulsion, that cannot be attributed to God; if it does not, then forcible prevention is outside His custom and not permissible. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that divine power implies arbitrary coercion in matters of faith.

Key Terms
إرادة
تمني
جبر
قسر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine will is similar to human wishful thinking, or that God's power to prevent disbelief implies He should force faith.
Correction: Divine will is effective and always prevails, while wishful thinking is impotent. Faith by coercion is an effect of confusion and is impermissible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is faith by coercion not permissible?
A) Because God does not have power over it.
B) Because will sometimes necessitates overcoming, but wishful thinking does not.
C) Because it is an effect of confusion and alienation.
D) Because it is outside of custom.

Key Takeaway
Divine will is effective and cannot be overcome by mere wishes; coerced faith is impermissible because it stems from confusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hope for something without effort—like faith in your heart without action—are you engaging in wishful thinking? How will you turn that hope into genuine submission to God's will today?
?
Have you ever wished that God would force someone you love to believe? What does this lesson's rejection of coerced faith teach you about the dignity of free choice?
?
In what area of your life do you secretly hold onto your own wishes while claiming to submit to God's will? What would it look like to truly align your desires with His effective will as described in this passage?

The Nature of Prevention and Coercion Refuted
Maturidi answers the objection about prevention and clarifies the role of cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God does not prevent all sin by force, and how prevention, when it occurs, is for a reason (ʿilla).

Core Idea
Prevention of sin is not a condition of divine will; it occurs only for a wise cause.

Maturidi continues by addressing a further objection: if God is wise and able, why does He not prevent His servant from doing what He does not will? The response clarifies that God does will the action (in terms of creation), and prevention is not a necessary condition. Moreover, prevention itself, when it happens, is always for a reason (ʿilla), not arbitrarily.

Guided Path
1
Read the next passage
This passage continues the argument. Read the Arabic and translation together.
It builds on the previous lesson.
2
Identify the objection
An objector says: a wise master prevents his servant from doing what he does not will. Why doesn't God do that?
3
Follow the reply
Maturidi refutes the objection: God does will the act (in a certain sense), and prevention is not a condition of will. He then adds that prevention is either due to a cause (ʿilla) or not; if due to a cause, it may necessitate compulsion, which cannot be attributed to God.
The sheikh adds that if you look at the witnessed world, prevention only occurs when the agent cannot do the act or does not will it.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The final sentence states that prevention without cause is outside God's custom and not permissible. Hence, God does not arbitrarily coerce.
This reinforces the Maturidi rejection of jabr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the passage, why does God not prevent His servant from sinning?

?

?

?
This lesson says prevention only occurs with a cause, and arbitrary coercion is outside God's custom. Look at your own life: is there a particular failure you have resented God for not stopping? Write down one such moment, then ask yourself: what wise purpose might that 'unprevented' act have served in your soul? Are you willing to let that purpose transform you instead of blaming God?

The Opponent's Claim of Arbitrary Guidance
Opponent's argument against initial divine guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's misinterpretation of Quranic guidance (هداية) as arbitrary and based on partiality, and why they reject the idea of initial guidance or misguidance.

Core Idea
Guidance is not arbitrary; the opponent's claim implies divine partiality.

The opponent begins by citing the verse "Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam" (6:125). They argue that the verse is understood to mean that God only gives guidance to those who already obey Him, and that He does not grant guidance or misguidance initially because that would imply partiality (هوادة) and favoritism (محاباة). This lesson presents the opponent's argument in their own words, setting the stage for Maturidi's refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's initial claim
Read the Arabic passage describing the opponent's interpretation of verse 6:125. Notice how they claim the verse refers to those who already obey God.
The opponent cites another verse (47:17) to support their view.
2
Identify the two reasons against initial guidance
The opponent gives two reasons why God cannot initially guide or misguide. Find these reasons in the text.
The reasons are based on God's nature (no partiality) and logical consistency (no blame).
3
Consider the opponent's underlying concern
The opponent believes that if God guides or misguides initially, it would imply injustice. Reflect on why this is problematic from their perspective.
This sets up the refutation on grounds of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في جواب ما عورض بقوله : فَمَنْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ، أن تأويله معروف وهو أن من أطاعه أتاه من لطائفه ما لا يقدر عليه غيره وسماه بالأسماء الشريفة وحكم له بالأحكام الرفيع ثوابا لطاعته ليزداد له الرغبة كقوله : وَالَّذِينَ اهتَدُوا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى ، ومن عصاه منع منه ما ذكر فيضيق صدره كا ولا يفعل بأحد ذلك إبتداء كالآية التي ذكرتها . وقوله : وَمَا يُضِلُّ بِهِ إِلَّا الْفَاسِقِينَ ، ثم قال : فلا يجوز ذلك ابتداء من غير استحقاق العداوة والولاية لأمرين: أحدهما أن ليس به هوادة ولا محاباة ، والثاني أن من يفرق عبيده بالحرف لم يكن له العود باللوم منهم على أحد . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أما ما ادعى على الآية أنها معروفة فهذا يدل على جهله بالمعروف والمنكر وقلبه القصة ، ثم أخطأ فى صرف الآية إلى ما بعد الإسلام المعروف من النطق، لأنه قال : فَمَنْ يُرِدْ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرُهُ الإِسْلَام فأثبت له الإسلام إذ شرح صدره لا أن شرح بعد أن وجد الإسلام ، ثم منه جرأته على الله أن مثل هذا يكون هوادة ومناجاة وما كان عليه إذ علم أعظم من صفته جرأته هذه في خاص نفسه أن لا يبدى ذلك ولا يعارض نفسه بما لا يضطر إليه، لكنه عوقب بجهله بالله وصرفه كتابة عن جهته طلبا لإقامة مذهب هو ينتج الزندقة ، فنعوذ بالله من الخذلان . ثم يقال : من أسلم وقت إسلامه أسلم وقليه مشروح له ، ووقت كفره قلبه ضيق ، أو هما واحد في الشرح والضيق . فإن قال : كانا واحدا ، ظهر كذبه عند كل من يحفظ ابتداء دينه من إسلام أو كفر ، ثم يسمى ما يعلم كذبه كل مسلم وكافر من الله هواده مرة ومحاباة ، بائنا وصدا عن الحق ومنعا ليعلموا جرأته وسفهه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم يقال له : الذي يريده بعد الإيمان أو يحرمه بعد الكفر ، وكان في ذلك معونة في الدين وتيسير عليه أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، بان بهته وسقط موضع جعل ذلك ثوابا أو عقابا ، وإن قال : بلى ، فقد أقر عليه مذهبه ببذل شيء هو أصلح له فى الدين. ثم يقال : هل رأيت كافرا بعد أن آمن ، أو أخبرت كون ذلك ، أو مؤمنا بعد الكفير ؟ لا بد من : بلى، قيل : أكان إعطاء الثواب ومنعه ذلك الشرح أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، ألزمه الخلف فى الوعد والكذب في الخبر ، وإن قال : نعم نعم ، قيل : أي نفع له في تلك الفوائد ، أو أي ضرر عليه في التضييق ؟ إذا ليجعل ذلك ثوابا أو عقابا ويمنع جواز ذلك ابتداء بما سماه مرة هوادة ومرة محاباة ومرة صدا ومرة منعا ، نسأل الله العصمة عن قول هذا عقباه
And he said in answer to what he was objected with by His saying: "Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam" (6:125) – that its interpretation is known, and it is that whoever obeys Him, He gives him of His subtleties what none other can give, and names him with the noble names, and decrees for him the sublime judgments as a reward for his obedience, to increase his desire, as His saying: "And those who are guided – He increases them in guidance" (47:17). And whoever disobeys Him, He withholds from him what was mentioned, so his breast becomes constricted, but He does not do that to anyone initially, like the verse you mentioned. And His saying: "And He misleads not thereby except the defiantly disobedient" (2:26). Then he said: So that is not permissible initially without deserving enmity or friendship, for two reasons: one, that there is no partiality or favoritism in Him, and second, that whoever distinguishes his servants by mere letters would not have the return of blame from them upon anyone. The Sheikh (may God have mercy on him) said: As for his claim that the verse is known, this indicates his ignorance of the known and the unknown and his turning over the story. Then he erred in diverting the verse to after the known Islam of speech, because he said: "Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam" – so he affirmed Islam for him when his breast was expanded, not that expansion occurred after finding Islam. Then from this is his audacity towards God that such a thing would be partiality and favoritism, and what was upon him when he knew – greater than his description – this audacity of his in his own self that he does not manifest that and does not oppose himself with what he is not compelled to, but he was punished by his ignorance of God and his turning aside from His Book seeking to establish a doctrine that produces heresy (zandaqah). So we seek refuge in God from abandonment. Then it is said: The one who became a Muslim at the time of his Islam – did he become a Muslim with his breast expanded, and at the time of his disbelief his breast was constricted, or are they the same in expansion and constriction? If he says: they were the same, his lie becomes apparent to everyone who knows the beginning of his religion, whether Islam or disbelief. Then he calls what every Muslim and disbeliever knows to be a lie from God – partiality sometimes, favoritism sometimes, turning away, hindrance from truth, and prevention – so that they may know his audacity and folly. And there is no power except through God. Then it is said to him: That which He wills after faith or deprives after disbelief – is there in that assistance in religion and facilitation upon it or not? If he says: No, his fabrication becomes apparent and the place of making that a reward or punishment falls. If he says: Yes, then he has affirmed his doctrine by bestowing something that is more beneficial for him in religion. Then it is said: Have you seen a disbeliever after he believed, or have you been informed of that, or a believer after disbelief? It must be: Yes. It is said: Was the giving of reward and its prevention that expansion or not? If he says: No, then he incurs the charge of breach of promise and lying in the report. If he says: Yes, yes, it is said: What benefit is there to him in those benefits, or what harm upon him in the constriction? Then let that be made a reward or punishment, and prohibit the permissibility of that initially by what he called once partiality, once favoritism, once hindrance, and once prevention. We ask God for protection from the consequence of this saying.
Source pages p. 899

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's misinterpretation of the Quranic verse about divine guidance (هداية) and misguidance (إضلال). The opponent argues that the verse implies God only guides those who are already Muslims and misguides others from the start. The author counters that the correct interpretation is that guidance is given as a reward for obedience, as in the verse 'He increases them in guidance' (47:17), and misguidance is a punishment for sin. The opponent claims that such a view implies partiality (هوادة) and favoritism (محاباة) on God's part. The author refutes this by stating that God's actions are based on merit (استحقاق), not arbitrary. The sheikh then launches a detailed critique, accusing the opponent of ignorance and audacity, and argues that the opponent's interpretation would lead to heresy (زندقة). The passage concludes with a series of dialectical questions exposing the inconsistency of the opponent's position: if guidance is a reward for faith, then the opponent's claim that God gives it arbitrarily collapses. The author thus upholds divine justice and the principle that rewards and punishments are based on deeds.

Key Terms
هداية
إضلال
استحقاق
هوادة
محاباة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God arbitrarily guides or misguides people without any reason, implying partiality.
Correction: The opponent themselves reject this, but Maturidi later shows that their interpretation also leads to problems. The correct view is that guidance is a reward for obedience and misguidance a punishment for sin.

Checkpoint
According to the opponent, what is the correct interpretation of the phrase 'Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam'?
A) It means God arbitrarily chooses whom to guide and whom to misguide.
B) It means God grants additional guidance as a reward for obedience.
C) It means God only guides those who are already Muslims.
D) It means God misguides people from the start.

Key Takeaway
The opponent argues that guidance is a reward for obedience, not an arbitrary gift, and that initial guidance would imply partiality in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own guidance, do you see it as a reward for something you did, or as a pure gift from God? How does this lesson challenge you to examine the role of your own choices in receiving divine favor?
?
Have you ever blamed God for not guiding someone you love? How does the opponent's argument in this passage change the way you think about God's justice in relation to human responsibility?
?
If guidance is truly a reward for obedience, what specific steps will you take today to increase your obedience so that you may receive more of His subtle favors?

Maturidi's Refutation: Guidance as Just Reward
Maturidi's refutation of the opponent's misinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the opponent's claim, including his critique of their ignorance, misquotation, and his dialectical proof that guidance is based on merit.

Core Idea
Divine guidance is justly given as reward; the opponent's charge of partiality is a symptom of deeper ignorance.

The sheikh (Maturidi) responds sharply to the opponent's argument. He accuses the opponent of ignorance and audacity for claiming that God's actions involve partiality. He then provides a detailed logical refutation, showing through a series of questions that the opponent's position leads to contradictions and undermines the very concept of reward and punishment. This lesson unpacks Maturidi's powerful critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the sheikh's initial critique
Read the passage where the sheikh dismisses the opponent's claim as ignorance. Notice his strong language and the accusation of misquoting the verse.
The sheikh points out that the verse says expansion to Islam, not after Islam.
2
Trace the dialectical questions
Maturidi poses a series of questions about the timing of expansion and constriction. Follow the logic: if the same person has expansion at Islam and constriction at disbelief, the opponent's claim fails.
This exposes the opponent's inconsistency.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the opponent's position leads to absurdity, such as accusing God of lying or breaching promises. The correct view is that guidance is a reward for faith.
The sheikh ends by seeking refuge from such erroneous speech.

وقال في جواب ما عورض بقوله : فَمَنْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ، أن تأويله معروف وهو أن من أطاعه أتاه من لطائفه ما لا يقدر عليه غيره وسماه بالأسماء الشريفة وحكم له بالأحكام الرفيع ثوابا لطاعته ليزداد له الرغبة كقوله : وَالَّذِينَ اهتَدُوا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى ، ومن عصاه منع منه ما ذكر فيضيق صدره كا ولا يفعل بأحد ذلك إبتداء كالآية التي ذكرتها . وقوله : وَمَا يُضِلُّ بِهِ إِلَّا الْفَاسِقِينَ ، ثم قال : فلا يجوز ذلك ابتداء من غير استحقاق العداوة والولاية لأمرين: أحدهما أن ليس به هوادة ولا محاباة ، والثاني أن من يفرق عبيده بالحرف لم يكن له العود باللوم منهم على أحد . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : أما ما ادعى على الآية أنها معروفة فهذا يدل على جهله بالمعروف والمنكر وقلبه القصة ، ثم أخطأ فى صرف الآية إلى ما بعد الإسلام المعروف من النطق، لأنه قال : فَمَنْ يُرِدْ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرُهُ الإِسْلَام فأثبت له الإسلام إذ شرح صدره لا أن شرح بعد أن وجد الإسلام ، ثم منه جرأته على الله أن مثل هذا يكون هوادة ومناجاة وما كان عليه إذ علم أعظم من صفته جرأته هذه في خاص نفسه أن لا يبدى ذلك ولا يعارض نفسه بما لا يضطر إليه، لكنه عوقب بجهله بالله وصرفه كتابة عن جهته طلبا لإقامة مذهب هو ينتج الزندقة ، فنعوذ بالله من الخذلان . ثم يقال : من أسلم وقت إسلامه أسلم وقليه مشروح له ، ووقت كفره قلبه ضيق ، أو هما واحد في الشرح والضيق . فإن قال : كانا واحدا ، ظهر كذبه عند كل من يحفظ ابتداء دينه من إسلام أو كفر ، ثم يسمى ما يعلم كذبه كل مسلم وكافر من الله هواده مرة ومحاباة ، بائنا وصدا عن الحق ومنعا ليعلموا جرأته وسفهه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم يقال له : الذي يريده بعد الإيمان أو يحرمه بعد الكفر ، وكان في ذلك معونة في الدين وتيسير عليه أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، بان بهته وسقط موضع جعل ذلك ثوابا أو عقابا ، وإن قال : بلى ، فقد أقر عليه مذهبه ببذل شيء هو أصلح له فى الدين. ثم يقال : هل رأيت كافرا بعد أن آمن ، أو أخبرت كون ذلك ، أو مؤمنا بعد الكفير ؟ لا بد من : بلى، قيل : أكان إعطاء الثواب ومنعه ذلك الشرح أو لا ؟ فإن قال : لا ، ألزمه الخلف فى الوعد والكذب في الخبر ، وإن قال : نعم نعم ، قيل : أي نفع له في تلك الفوائد ، أو أي ضرر عليه في التضييق ؟ إذا ليجعل ذلك ثوابا أو عقابا ويمنع جواز ذلك ابتداء بما سماه مرة هوادة ومرة محاباة ومرة صدا ومرة منعا ، نسأل الله العصمة عن قول هذا عقباه
And he said in answer to what he was objected with by His saying: "Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam" (6:125) – that its interpretation is known, and it is that whoever obeys Him, He gives him of His subtleties what none other can give, and names him with the noble names, and decrees for him the sublime judgments as a reward for his obedience, to increase his desire, as His saying: "And those who are guided – He increases them in guidance" (47:17). And whoever disobeys Him, He withholds from him what was mentioned, so his breast becomes constricted, but He does not do that to anyone initially, like the verse you mentioned. And His saying: "And He misleads not thereby except the defiantly disobedient" (2:26). Then he said: So that is not permissible initially without deserving enmity or friendship, for two reasons: one, that there is no partiality or favoritism in Him, and second, that whoever distinguishes his servants by mere letters would not have the return of blame from them upon anyone. The Sheikh (may God have mercy on him) said: As for his claim that the verse is known, this indicates his ignorance of the known and the unknown and his turning over the story. Then he erred in diverting the verse to after the known Islam of speech, because he said: "Whomsoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam" – so he affirmed Islam for him when his breast was expanded, not that expansion occurred after finding Islam. Then from this is his audacity towards God that such a thing would be partiality and favoritism, and what was upon him when he knew – greater than his description – this audacity of his in his own self that he does not manifest that and does not oppose himself with what he is not compelled to, but he was punished by his ignorance of God and his turning aside from His Book seeking to establish a doctrine that produces heresy (zandaqah). So we seek refuge in God from abandonment. Then it is said: The one who became a Muslim at the time of his Islam – did he become a Muslim with his breast expanded, and at the time of his disbelief his breast was constricted, or are they the same in expansion and constriction? If he says: they were the same, his lie becomes apparent to everyone who knows the beginning of his religion, whether Islam or disbelief. Then he calls what every Muslim and disbeliever knows to be a lie from God – partiality sometimes, favoritism sometimes, turning away, hindrance from truth, and prevention – so that they may know his audacity and folly. And there is no power except through God. Then it is said to him: That which He wills after faith or deprives after disbelief – is there in that assistance in religion and facilitation upon it or not? If he says: No, his fabrication becomes apparent and the place of making that a reward or punishment falls. If he says: Yes, then he has affirmed his doctrine by bestowing something that is more beneficial for him in religion. Then it is said: Have you seen a disbeliever after he believed, or have you been informed of that, or a believer after disbelief? It must be: Yes. It is said: Was the giving of reward and its prevention that expansion or not? If he says: No, then he incurs the charge of breach of promise and lying in the report. If he says: Yes, yes, it is said: What benefit is there to him in those benefits, or what harm upon him in the constriction? Then let that be made a reward or punishment, and prohibit the permissibility of that initially by what he called once partiality, once favoritism, once hindrance, and once prevention. We ask God for protection from the consequence of this saying.

God's Conclusive Argument Refutes the Polytheists' Excuse
Maturidi cites Quran 6:149 to refute the polytheists' excuse of divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'To Allah belongs the conclusive argument' refutes the polytheists' claim that their disbelief was by God's will.

Core Idea
God's conclusive argument leaves no excuse for disbelief.

This lesson focuses on a crucial verse that Maturidi uses to seal the refutation of the polytheists. They claimed that their shirk was by God's will. In response, the verse declares that the final proof belongs to Allah alone, and if He had willed, He would have guided all. But His will does not justify their disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its concise style. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
The passage cites the end of a verse from Surah Al-An'am.
2
Identify how the verse is cited
Notice that Maturidi says 'that is supported by the end of the verse'. This shows he is using the Quran as evidence for his previous arguments.
3
Understand 'conclusive argument'
The phrase 'To Allah belongs the conclusive argument' means that God has the ultimate proof that leaves no room for valid excuse. Reflect on how this refutes the polytheists' claim.
The argument is decisive and clear.
4
Reflect on the conditional statement
The verse adds 'if He had willed, He would have guided you all'. This shows that God's will could have forced guidance, but He chose to send messengers instead. Polytheists cannot use divine will as an excuse.
The conditional indicates that God's actual will does not compel belief.
5
Connect to the lesson's main idea
Bring together the two parts: the conclusive argument proves the polytheists wrong, and the conditional shows that their excuse is invalid. Summarize how the passage refutes the claim about will.
This is the core teaching of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أيد ذلك آخر الآية: {قُلْ فَلِلَّهِ الْحُجَّةُ الْبَالِغَةُ فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ}. وغير ذلك، ولا يحتمل لما مر بيانه.
That is supported by the end of the verse: {Say, 'To Allah belongs the conclusive argument. For if He had willed, He would have guided you all.'} And other than that, and it does not allow what has passed of its explanation.
Source pages p. 901

Commentary
This passage cites the latter part of the same verse (Quran 6:149) to reinforce the refutation. The author says that the end of the verse supports the previous three responses. The conclusive argument belongs to God alone, and if He had willed, He would have guided all. This shows that the polytheists cannot use divine will as an excuse because God's actual guidance is not universal in the sense of forcing belief. The passage also notes that the verse 'does not allow' the interpretation the polytheists gave, as already explained.

Key Terms
الحجة البالغة (conclusive argument)
هداية (guidance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'if He willed, He would have guided you all' implies God does not want guidance for all.
Correction: The phrase refers to a type of will that would compel faith, not God's actual will to guide through evidence and choice. God does want guidance for all but allows freedom.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'Say: To Allah belongs the conclusive argument' indicate?
A) God has no argument against disbelievers.
B) God's will can excuse disbelief.
C) God has the final proof, so the polytheists' excuse is invalid.
D) All people are forced to believe.

Key Takeaway
The verse establishes that God's proof is decisive and that His will does not excuse disbelief; rather, guidance comes through His sending of messengers and evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Coercive Will vs. Test in Q.10:99
Maturidi interprets Q.10:99 as referring to coercive will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's distinction between coercive will and ordinary will in interpreting Q.10:99.

Core Idea
God's will to force belief is not His ordinary will—He wills to test.

This lesson explores Maturidi's interpretation of a key verse often misunderstood to imply universal determinism. Maturidi clarifies that God could force everyone to believe, but He chooses not to, instead testing humanity. The passage distinguishes between coercive will and the will that permits free choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic verse and translation
Read the Arabic passage from Maturidi's commentary along with the literal translation. Notice the key terms: إكراه, قسر, ابتلاء.
The verse is from Surah Yunus (10:99).
2
Identify the key concepts
Identify what 'will of compulsion' (مشيئة القسر) means and how it contrasts with the will to test (ابتلاء). Maturidi says that with coercive will there is no praise or reward.
3
Contrast with the common misunderstanding
Reflect on the common misunderstanding that this verse proves God forces all to believe. Maturidi shows it is about a hypothetical coercive will, not actual will.
This guards against determinist interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في قوله تعالى: {وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَنْ فِي الْأَرْضِ كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا}، إنه على الإكراه قسرًا جعلهم شيوخًا وشبابًا، ولكن شاء أن يبتليهم كقوله: {وَلَوْ يَشَاءُ اللَّهُ لَانْتَصَرَ}، وقد شاء ذلك بالنبي وأصحابه، ولكن أراد به مشيئة القسر، إذ ليس معها حمد ولا أجر.
And He said regarding His saying Exalted: {And if your Lord had willed, all on earth would have believed — all of them entirely}, that it is upon coercion, forcefully making them old and young, but He willed to test them, like His saying: {And if Allah had willed, He could have taken vengeance} — and He has willed that for the Prophet and his companions, but He intended by it a will of compulsion, for there is no praise or reward with it.
Source pages p. 901

Commentary
This passage addresses the verse from Surah Yunus (10:99). The author interprets it as referring to a will of coercion (مشيئة القسر), where God could force everyone to believe by making them old or young (a change of state), but He did not will that. Instead, He willed to test them. The author compares this to the verse from Surah Muhammad (47:4) about God being able to take vengeance. The point is that God's will is not always the same; He wills compulsion in some matters, but in the case of human free will, He does not force belief. This guards against the misunderstanding that God's will for faith would negate human responsibility.

Key Terms
مشيئة القسر (coercive will)
ابتلاء (test)
إكراه (compulsion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this verse proves God wills all to believe in a determinist sense, i.e., everyone is forced to believe.
Correction: The author clarifies it is a conditional will of compulsion (coercive will), not actual will. God chooses not to force belief in order to test humanity.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi mean by 'will of compulsion' (مشيئة القسر)?
A) God forces all to believe.
B) God could force belief but chooses not to, in order to test.
C) God's will is always coercive.
D) The verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that God's will to force belief is different from His will that allows testing; only the latter involves reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel your faith is weak, do you secretly wish God would just force you to believe perfectly? How does this lesson expose the danger of that wish?
?
God wills to test you rather than coerce you. What does that say about the value of your sincere efforts in worship, even when they feel small?
?
If there is no reward in being forced to obey, then what is the state of your heart when you perform an act of worship? Are you seeking reward through your own free choice, or just going through motions?

Refutation of the Mu'tazila Claim on God's Power
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila claim on human acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila claim that God cannot create human acts, using Quranic verses to affirm God's absolute power and will.

Core Idea
God's power encompasses all creation, including human acts.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid confronts a key Mu'tazila doctrine: that God cannot create the actions of human beings. Maturidi argues that this contradicts the clear Quranic testimony of God's unlimited power and sovereign will. Through a series of Quranic proofs, he demonstrates that God's ability to create all things—including human acts—is beyond question.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Maturidi's argument flow. Notice the citation of three Quranic verses.
The passage contains some textual uncertainties due to OCR.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Find where Maturidi states the Mu'tazila position and their reasoning. They claimed that God cannot create human acts.
3
Understand the Quranic responses
See how each verse addresses a different aspect of the claim: (1) general power, (2) will to guide, (3) will to take vengeance. These prove God's complete control.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why this refutation is crucial for the Islamic understanding of God's omnipotence and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: وقد بينا ما يدل على وهمه، على أنه من كان يظن أن الله يعجز عن هذا النوع من الخلق، ولا على حقيقة فعل الخلق، بل لو أريد ذا لكان موضعه نيا ظن المعتزلة أنهم خلقوا خلقا ليس في العقول أرفع منه ولا أعلى في الحسن والفضل. فرمت هذا المعتزلة على ألسن الضعفة، فبين الله قدرته على مثل ذلك، وإلا لا وجه لإنكار مثله ممن يقر له بخلق السماوات والأرض وما بينها، ولكن بين بذلك فساد قول المعتزلة: إن الله قد شاء، فلم يكن، إذ هو لا يقدر على خلق أفعال العباد، فقال: وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، جوابا لذلك، وقال تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاء لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ جوابا للأول، وقوله: وَلَوْ يَشَاءُ اللَّهُ لَانْتَصَرَ مِنْهُم، أنه لو شاء تكذيب منذريه، بل لا يشاء لا نتصر منهم بما شاء، ولكن شاء التأخير، والثالث لانتصر منهم يهم، ولكن شاء أن يبلو صحابة نبيه بالهزيمة ليبين الذين صدقوا كقوله تعالى: وَلَقَدْ فَتَنَّا الَّذِينَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِمْ، وقوله: وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَنْ يَعْبُدُ اللَّهَ عَلَى حَرْفٍ.
The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: And we have shown what indicates his illusion, that whoever thinks that Allah is incapable of this type of creation, nor of the reality of the act of creation, but if this were intended, its place would be... the Mu'tazila thought that they created a creation not higher in intellects nor higher in goodness and virtue. The Mu'tazila threw this upon the tongues of the weak, so Allah showed His power over the like of that, otherwise there is no reason to deny the like of it from one who affirms for Him the creation of the heavens and the earth and what is between them, but He showed by that the corruption of the Mu'tazila's statement: 'Indeed Allah willed, but it did not happen, because He is not able to create the acts of the servants.' So He said: 'And He is over all things competent' (Quran 11:4) as a response to that, and He said: 'But if He willed, He would have guided you all' (Quran 6:149) as a response to the first, and His saying: 'And if Allah willed, He could have taken vengeance upon them' (Quran 47:4) that if He willed, He would have belied His warners, but He does not will to take vengeance upon them by what He wills, but He wills delay, and the third... but He willed to test the companions of His Prophet with defeat to show those who were truthful, as His saying: 'And We have certainly tried those before them' (Quran 29:3), and His saying: 'And among the people is he who worships Allah on an edge' (Quran 22:11).
Source pages p. 902

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila claim that God cannot create the acts of His servants. The author begins by stating that he has already shown what indicates the error of this view. He then describes the Mu'tazila's position: they thought that they themselves created a type of creation that is considered the highest in intellect and virtue. They spread this idea among the weak. In response, God demonstrated His power over such creation, implying that it is unreasonable for someone who acknowledges that God created the heavens and the earth to deny His power over similar acts. The author then presents three Quranic verses as evidence: (1) 'He is over all things competent' (11:4) as a direct response to the claim that God cannot create acts, (2) 'If He willed, He would have guided you all' (6:149) to show His absolute will, and (3) 'If Allah willed, He could have taken vengeance upon them' (47:4) to indicate that if He willed, He could have destroyed the disbelievers, but He wills delay and testing. The author concludes by citing verses about testing and those who worship on an edge to emphasize God's complete control and wisdom.

فعل العباد
المعتزلة
مشيئة
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God is incapable of creating human acts, so human acts are created by humans themselves.
Correction: The passage refutes this by citing Quranic verses that affirm God's absolute power over all things, including human acts, and that His will is sovereign.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the Mu'tazila claim that the author refutes?
A) God does not know human actions.
B) God cannot create the acts of His servants.
C) God is unjust in commanding obedience.
D) God's will is irrelevant to human actions.

Key Takeaway
God's power is absolute and encompasses all creation, including human acts, as affirmed by Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's power encompasses every action you take, including your words and thoughts? What would change in your daily life if you lived with this conviction moment by moment?
?
The Mu'tazila arrogantly claimed to create something superior. Where in your own heart do you subtly attribute your successes, talents, or virtues to yourself rather than to Allah's creation and permission?
?
If Allah willed, He could end your test right now. Are you living in grateful awareness that every breath of delay is His wisdom and mercy, or do you presume upon His patience as if you deserve more time?

Why Willing Sins Is Not Evil While Commanding Them Is
Maturidi gives multiple rational arguments distinguishing divine will from divine command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational distinction between divine will and divine command, and why willing sins does not entail ugliness while commanding them does.

Core Idea
Command changes the nature of an act; will does not.

Maturidi addresses a subtle objection: if commanding evil is bad, why is willing evil not also bad? The answer lies in the fundamental difference between command and will—command transforms a sin into obedience, while will leaves the act unchanged. This lesson unpacks the reasons he gives, showing how each demonstrates the distinct roles of these divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the flow from the objection to the multiple answers introduced by 'قيل لوجوه' and 'وأيضا'.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection and first reason
The objector asks why willing sins is not ugly if commanding them is. The first reason given: commanding a sin would make it obedience, which is contradictory. Notice how will does not have this effect.
This is the core distinction.
3
Follow the additional reasons
Maturidi gives several more 'أيضا' reasons: God's will for prophets' destruction, the purpose of command vs will, and the story of Abraham. List each reason in your mind.
Each reason builds the case.
4
Reflect on the Abraham example
The story of Abraham and the ram shows that command and will are distinct: God commanded the sacrifice but did not intend its actual occurrence, otherwise preventing it would imply ignorance.
This is a concrete proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل: إذ قبح الأمر بالمعاصي لما لا قبح إرادة كونها؟ قيل لوجوه: أحدها التناقض فى الأمر، وليس ذلك فى الإرادة لأن الفعل يصير للأمر، فمحال الأمر بالمعصية لأنه يصير بالأمر طاعة، فيبطل معنى المعصية بها الأمر، وليست الإرادة كذلك. ألا يرى أن كل فاعل مريد لفعله ومحال أن يقال: أمر نفسه بفعله، ثبت أنهما مختلفان، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن الله يوصف بالإرادة فى فعله، ومحال أن يكون عليه أمر فيه، فثبت أن أحد الوجهين ليس هو دليل الآخر. مع ما كان الله تعالى مريدا هلاك الأنبياء والأخيار وبقاء الأعداء والأشرار والسعة لهؤلاء في الدنيا، ولم يأمر بذلك، بل أمرنا بالدعاء بهلاك هؤلاء وبقاء أولئك، والله الموفق. وأيضا إن فائدة الأمر رفعة الأمر وعلوه حيث استبعد الآخر وأظهر فيه حقه وعظيم مننه التي بها استحق أن يكون سيدا له ومعبودا، وحق الإرادة الاختيار ونفى الغلبة أن لا يقهر ولا يمنع عن سلطانه ولا يحال بينه وبين ملكه، وفى دفع الإرادة هذا. لذلك بطل أن لا يريد، وكذلك في المنع عن الأمر والنهي؛ لذلك لزم القول بالأمر والنهى على الأمرين ليظهر سلطانه وربوبيته، ولزم الإرادة فى الكل ليحق ملكه وعجز الخلق من أن يريدوا في ملكه وسلطانه، والله الموفق. وأيضا إن الله أمر ابراهيم بالذبح وفداء بالكبش، فلا يجوز أن يكون أراد فعل حقيقة الذبح ثم يمنع عنه بالبدل؛ لأنه آية البداء وعلامة الجهل، فكان الأمر لا بالذى به حقيقة الأرادة، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
If a questioner says: 'Since commanding sins is ugly, why is there no ugliness in willing their occurrence?' It is said for reasons: One of them is the contradiction in command, and that is not in will, because the act becomes according to the command, so commanding a sin is impossible because it becomes obedience by the command, so the meaning of sin is nullified by the command, and will is not like that. Do you not see that every doer is willing his act, and it is impossible to say: He commanded himself to do his act. So it is established that they are different, and there is no power except through Allah. Also, Allah is described by will in His act, and it is impossible that there should be a command over Him in it, so it is established that one aspect is not a proof for the other. Moreover, Allah is willing the destruction of prophets and the righteous and the survival of enemies and the wicked and abundance for these in the world, and He did not command that, but He commanded us to supplicate for the destruction of these and the survival of those, and Allah is the grantor of success. Also, the benefit of command is the elevation and loftiness of the commander, where He distances the other and shows His right and great blessings by which He deserves to be a lord and worshipped, and the right of will is choice and denial of compulsion, so that He is not overcome nor prevented from His authority, nor is there to be any bar between Him and His kingdom. In repelling will this... Therefore it is invalid that He does not will, and similarly regarding prevention of command and prohibition; therefore it is necessary to affirm command and prohibition on the two matters to manifest His authority and lordship, and it is necessary to affirm will in all to realize His kingdom and the inability of creatures to will in His kingdom and authority, and Allah is the grantor of success. Also, Allah commanded Abraham to sacrifice and ransomed with a ram, so it is not permissible that He intended the actual act of slaughter and then prevented him from it with a substitute, because that would be a sign of reconsideration (bada') and a mark of ignorance. So the command was not based on the reality of intention, and there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 903

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks: 'If commanding sins is ugly, why is not willing their occurrence also ugly?' The answer is given with multiple reasons. First, there is a contradiction in command because an act becomes obedience by the command; if God commanded a sin, it would become obedience, nullifying sin. Will, however, does not change the act. Every agent wills his own act, but one cannot command oneself. This shows they differ. Second, God is described as having will regarding His own act, but He cannot be commanded concerning it, so will and command are distinct. Third, God wills the destruction of prophets and survival of enemies, but He does not command these; He commands us to pray for the opposite. Fourth, the purpose of command is to show the commander's authority and the subject's obligation, while the purpose of will is to show God's absolute sovereignty without compulsion. Therefore, both command and will are necessary to manifest different aspects of God's lordship. Finally, the story of Abraham's sacrifice shows that God commanded the sacrifice but did not intend its actual occurrence, as He provided a ransom; otherwise, preventing it after intending it would imply ignorance. Thus, command and will are distinct.

Key Terms
الأمر
الإرادة
المعصية
طاعة
البداء
الاختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since commanding evil is bad, willing evil is also bad.
Correction: Command changes the nature of an act—a commanded sin becomes obedience—while will does not. Therefore, willing sins is not ugly, as it does not alter the act's moral status.

Checkpoint
What is the first reason given for why willing sin is not like commanding sin?
A) Will is hidden while command is public.
B) Commanding a sin makes it obedience, so it is impossible; will does not.
C) God only wills good things.
D) The objector is mistaken from the start.

Key Takeaway
Command and will are distinct divine attributes; commanding sins is impossible because it would change their nature, while willing them does not, and both serve different purposes in manifesting God's lordship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you subtly excuse yourself by thinking that God willed it? How does knowing that His command prohibits it while His will may permit it change your personal responsibility? Will you stop using 'God willed it' as an excuse and instead hold yourself accountable to His command?
?
The passage says God wills the destruction of the righteous but commands you to pray for them. Does your prayer feel like it can change God's will, or are you simply obeying His command? How does this distinction affect the urgency and sincerity of your supplications? Are you praying to change outcomes, or to align with His command?
?
If command shows God's right to be worshipped and will shows His absolute sovereignty, which aspect do you focus on in your daily life? Are you more concerned with obeying His commands as an act of worship, or do you merely acknowledge His will passively? What would change if you saw every command as a direct invitation to exalt Him as your Lord?
